\mbox{\Hypertarget{_0dbabel_2parser_2lib_2index_8js_a6fd05206266746979959a2bac1f80a2b}\label{_0dbabel_2parser_2lib_2index_8js_a6fd05206266746979959a2bac1f80a2b}} 
\index{index.js@{index.js}!parse@{parse}}
\index{parse@{parse}!index.js@{index.js}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{parse}{parse}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{shared_2rollup_8js_ab94e0a6507d6af3464617b932a6a041a}{picomatch}} parse = parse}



internal Markdown\+It.\+parse(src, env) -\/$>$ Array 

\mbox{\hyperlink{classParse}{Parse}} the given {\ttfamily str} with the given {\ttfamily options}.

\mbox{\hyperlink{classParse}{Parse}} a glob pattern to create the source string for a regular expression.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item src (String)\+: source string
\item env (Object)\+: environment sandbox
\end{DoxyItemize}

\mbox{\hyperlink{classParse}{Parse}} input string and return list of block tokens (special token type \char`\"{}inline\char`\"{} will contain list of inline tokens). You should not call this method directly, until you write custom renderer (for example, to produce A\+ST).

{\ttfamily env} is used to pass data between \char`\"{}distributed\char`\"{} rules and return additional metadata like reference info, needed for the renderer. It also can be used to inject data in specific cases. Usually, you will be ok to pass {\ttfamily \{\}}, and then pass updated object to renderer.
